You're on a hill, behind you your family in front of you the approaching forces. You say your good-byes despite the pleading for you to come with them, but you know you have to stay. You tell them that you love them and to go and not look back . You turn to face the approaching horde, there are so many but you must do this. You look back one last time to ensure that they will be safe. Then you look up to the sky  and look at the rising sun. It's time, you light a cigarette take a drag and then pick up your rifle. You lock and load, you say one last prayer and then steady your aim. You won't win this fight but you sure as hell will take a few with you. You start dropping them, one by one they fall. You take a hit in the leg and you stumble, but you have to do this, to protect the ones you love. You reload another magazine and continue firing, but there are so many of them, too many for one man. But the hell with it, you scream, you laugh like a madman and you taunt them as you bring them low. You take another hit, this time in the shoulder. You aim is unsteady, you can barely think but you think of your family and that gives you strength. Bloodied , you hold your rifle one handed, you manage to take a few more. As you are changing the magazine you get hit in the chest, it knocks the wind out of you, you can taste blood. Your strength is sapped, you fall hard . You know that this is it. You look one more time towards the horizon, you don't see your loved ones, they are safe. As you look up to the fading sky, you think of your wife and how beautiful she was, you think of your son and how he will make you proud, you think of your daughter and how kind hearted she was. Your body goes numb, you feel cold, it won't be long now, you can hear the approach of the enemy, their heavy foot falls echoing. You think to yourself that you led a good life and you know that you were loved. As you see the enemy moving forward, you pull the pin from one of your grenades. The enemy surrounds you, you laugh a last laugh, more like coughing. The enemy mocks you in a language you don't understand. As one of them moves towards you, he moves to grab your weapon. You grab his arm before he can do so .You look him in the eyes and smile. This is from my family you say just as the grenade explodes. You die with a glad heart and with fury in your veins knowing that your family will live one.

A few years ago, I was working as a pizza delivery guy in a small town in the Northern US. I had an order to a motel, and while trying to find the motel room I needed to deliver to, I passed by the pool where a bunch of younger guys (early 20s) were swimming and relaxing, with a radio playing some song. That song ended, and the first bars to this song started playing. EVERYONE in the pool area got genuinely excited and started shouting and cheering.  Since then, I came up with the "Freebird Index", as a method to tell how "Southern" a place is. Go to a sufficiently populated group of random people, start playing this song, and gauge the reaction. The more excited the group gets, the more "Southern" the area is.

I have worked hard for many years to make the LGBT community to take possession of this song. There is no reason it should not be theirs, but a lot of them are afraid of it, it feels oppressive to them. It shouldn't. Freedom to be who you are is the heart of this song, but a lot of them don't see it that way. They see it as the song of the person who beat them down, but that's not his song, he has no ownership of it. Freedom does not oppress others, No free bird ever kept another bird from flying. I hope someday that the community understands, Freedom only lifts, it never oppresses, and there is so much beauty when freedom lifts more people to new heights.

This song means so much to me. I went to prison in 2020 and when they were transporting us from country jail to the actual prison and the prison was coming into view this song started playing. We were all joking around and trying to keep our spirits up and take our minds off the fact we were gonna be here for a couple years, then as we made it to the top of the hill the prison came into view at the same exact time that this fucking song came on. The whole bus went dead silent immediately, everyone fell silent and stared out the windows or down at the cuffs around their wrists and fetters around their ankle. The good vibes were crushed into oblivion, the depression that swept into the bus was suffocating, stunning even the hardest of criminals on the bus. One man had a tear roll down his face.  That shit hurt so bad. the absolute worst song to be playing while youâ€™re shackled up driving through multiple fences at a maximum security facility.  As I was walking from the back of the bus to the front before getting off the song was around 4:43 and it really helped me shake off the emotions, leave my feelings on the bus and get myself war-ready.  The timing of the song and the prison coming into view and switching up as I was walking from the back of the bus to the front was absolutely perfect, like it was scene from a movie.  And itâ€™s not like the transport officers played this song on purpose it was on the radio. That moment was so incredibly painful, yet so beautiful.  0/10 would not recommend.

I picked Leon Wilkeson up at his house on Ernest st. In riverside, jacksonville in 1996. I was 16 and the girl i liked's dad was high school buddies with him. He asked me to pick him up and bring him out with us to shoot pool. My green a%% picked him up in my black 88 mustang and he said DETOUR!!!, straight to "Whites Bar". A bar surrounded by barbed wire and cameras where the bartender was cleaning his shotgun on the bar when we walked thru the door. Then he made me pick up some shrimp from "Mary-annes golden fried chicken." Then we went to my girls house to get her and her dad. Went and shot a few games at "TJ's Bar". A few days later i get a call from Leon. I picked him up and brought him to my house where we proceded with a jam session. Two guitars rockin "Gimmie three steps" and "Tuesday's gone" Then he asked for a drink so i gave him all we had was blue curacao. He drank the whole bottle. Later my 20 year old, much more talented brother showed up and they started playing. Im 44 now and couldn't fully understand how bad-ass an experience i was having back then. RIP Leon.

Me
Recorded at Quinvy '70. Marlin Greene engineered. I was in the studio, sang on their audition that day using my songs. Part of "The Lost Tapes". Ronnie on bass, Leon couldn't make the trip. This is the track that got them signed to Capricorn. I was in the office when David Johnson played it for Phil Walden. He listened twice, got up, into his silver Lincoln, drove to Jacksonville and signed them.

"Free Bird," with its themes of freedom and escape, undoubtedly resonated with many Vietnam War veterans who faced immense challenges upon returning home. The song's powerful guitar solo and poignant lyrics could offer a momentary sense of solace and liberation as they dealt with their pain and sought comfort on the open road. It should never be trivialized as a meme. Van Zandt and others lost their lives when the song propelled them to iconic statusâ€”a status they will forever hold. Released on their debut album in 1973, they passed away just as they were beginning to enjoy the fame it brought them, never fully realizing the impact this song would have on their fans and other bands and future generations should treat it the same.

Those lyrics - "If I leave here tomorrow, would you still remember me" - breaks my heart knowing that was just a few months before the plane crash ğŸ’” And not only that.  According to former bandmate Artimus Pyle and family members, Ronnie Van Zant frequently discussed his mortality. Pyle recalls a moment when Lynyrd Skynyrd was in Japan: "Ronnie and I were in Tokyo, Japan, and Ronnie told me that he would never live to see thirty and that he would go out with his boots on, in other words, on the road. I said, 'Ronnie, don't talk like that,' but the man knew his destiny.] Van Zant's father, Lacy, said, "He said to me many times, 'Daddy, I'll never be 30 years old.' I said, 'Why are you talking this junk? You will never be 30 years old?' and he said, 'Daddy, that's my limit.' " Van Zant's father later noted that, "God was a jealous god. Taking him for reasons I don't know. Ex-bandmate Ed King also reported hearing Van Zant saying he would never live to be 30, saying Van Zant said it so often that he "had gotten sick of hearing it". Lynyrd Skynyrd backup singer JoJo Billingsley recalled that Van Zant had begun referring to himself as "The Mississippi Kid" in the months before his death despite being born and raised in Florida. She noted that, eerily, Van Zant's only connection to Mississippi was that he would ultimately die there.  His death was just meant to be... It's seriously f#%@!ked up when you think about it.

'' Dad, why do you listen to this song, we are not even American.''  '' Come here son, let me tell you a story, of the greatest song ever written. '' '' It all started with this amazing group of random souls brought together across thousands of miles across this tiny rock, in this intergalactic ocean, we are but a drop. Every once in a while a Ripple is created that echoes and shatters across the surface of the planet, breaking through time and space and language. Every once in a while you learn how to get high, from a gradual incremental hit to a full throttle gas pedal smashed into the fucking carpet ride, next thing you know your down the motor way, red lining the engine, bouncing the needle like its on a trampoline. And then it happens, you meet another soul who delights and revels in the same utter chaos that your soul cries out for. In that moment of utter and crazy high, something primordial sparks and your set on a journey that neither you nor she planned for.  We don't need to be American to enjoy the best song ever written, that's the beauty and power of this song. Learn to be happy and love your neighbour, that's the most we can expect for in this ride that is life.

I read opinions calling this the "best guitar solo of all time" here. I don't like the notion of "best solo". This song and its solos are iconic and very good, by all means, but everybody has their own feeling about the guitar solo(s) they like best, and from a purely technical point of view, there are certainly better ones. But speed is not everything, feeling, the interplay like here, and other factors. As for me, there are quite a few solos by Thin Lizzy guitarists that I would prefer, but this is only my personal opinion, of course. So let's put down these "the best... of all time" claims, they are pointless.

My sons favorite was Free ird because he loved his Free Dom to go places do things . He loved it too much. His freedom got him killed . Lake Worth Rd I hated when he was a child. He got a three wheeler and went behind cars on Lake Worth Rd . Lady came to my house not far from that Rd and told me she almost killed my son and to get him off that Rd. Michael was such a FreeBird free spirit when he grew up he still loved his freedom on Lake Worth Rd. I called him from another city from him and he was alone in his apartment . He said he had a cold and needed to go to the store. The convenient store was on Lake Worth Rd. Before I hung up with him I told him I loved him ( as his mother) He said Huh ! Like why did I have to say it.. Later on about an hour had past I got a call from the highway patrol and he told me that my son was killed by a Honda truck because that truck had long  iron pipes hanging out of the back of the truck . My son didn't use a car but his bicycle. No trails for bikes to ride safely on so he having no fear of Lake Worth Rd was pierced in the head with those pipes. He died instantly. The funeral home sent me a tiny letter full of him that's all that's left of Michael. He's freedom will be forever. I listen to Lynrd Skynrds FreeBird to get closer to my invisible son . I feel him in my heart. The man with the Honda truck wasn't charged. I have yet to find out details of this that shouldn't have happened. You lose your only son you lost part of your being as a human being. He would have protested Trump because he's an authority dictator minded person . Poor excuse for a human being. Love your son's every day tell them you love them when they leave your sight as they might not come back. Thanks for reading . I'm ok but think of him every time I here the word Freedom. He stood for freedom. He is a FreeBird now.

A hunk of metal, but more just than metal, She had a soul.  So i drove her to the location of the buyer.  Put on a playlist, and this song was the encore for the ride. For a moment there, someone or something  was there and played the song at the right moment.  I Was under the speed limit, because she was too scary to drive fast with, she rustled so damn hard at 3000 Rpm. When i got to a tunnel at the highway, the solo kicked in. I drove so goddamn hard while screaming to the solo ( "Lord i can't change") .. At that moment, i was free. No Other cars behind or front of me. No one to witness the aesthetic experience, just her and me.   No chains or rope  to claim bondage. I was a free man.  If i die here, i die happy. My car, and me. Together forever. I don't care.   I can easily say, that i cried so much when the song faded out.  I Miss that girl, one of a kind.

Thank you for one of the best memories I will every have.... As we journeyed home from an exhilarating robotics competition, the hum of the bus was suddenly pierced by the unmistakable strains of "Free bird." Instantly, my friend Harry and I locked eyes, sharing an unspoken understanding as the iconic melody ignited a spark within us. With infectious energy, we began to sing along, our voices intertwining with the music's soul-stirring lyrics. It started with just a the two of us singing along, but as the iconic riff approached, more and more voices joined in, and soon the bus was alive with the sound of everyone singing and grooving to the music. As the iconic riff kicked in, a wave of energy swept through the bus. Heads violently bobbed as everyone surrendered to the infectious groove of the song, fully immersed in the moment. Although this may have happened just yesterday, I know this song will bring me back every time I hear it.

Me playing war thunder and listening
This song just unlocked something in me. My mom died unexpectedly in July, and when the guitar solo kicked in I just started sobbing more uncontrollably than I have since she passed. We're from Jacksonville, home of LS, and my mom and her brothers would have been in their late-teens and twenties when Skynyrd was coming up in the early 70s.  She's from a big family, and a number of her brothers and sisters (my uncles and aunts) have been passing in recent years. It's easy to imagine them back in the day heading to a Skynyrd show in Jax, drinking beer in the parking lot, and letting loose to this same solo. I'm 34 now and grew up listening to Lynyrd Skynyrd, and this song has always been energizing, emotional, and powerful. I haven't listened to it fully in years, you hear a song so many times you think you know it as well as you can. But this time around, it really messed me up and got me feeling all sorts of profound things. Thanks! RIP Mom, David, Robby, Al, Margaret <3
